<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cambridgeshire_guided_busway.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Cambridgeshire_guided_busway.png/220px-Cambridgeshire_guided_busway.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Cambridgeshire_guided_busway.png/330px-Cambridgeshire_guided_busway.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Cambridgeshire_guided_busway.png/440px-Cambridgeshire_guided_busway.png 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="719" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cambridgeshire_guided_busway.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cambridgeshire Guided Busway network between Huntingdon (top-left) and Cambridge (bottom-right)</div></div></div>
<p>Starting at <a href="/wiki/Huntingdon_railway_station" title="Huntingdon railway station">Huntingdon railway station</a> and town centre, buses travel on normal roads to St Ives. From here the busway follows the path of the former <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_and_Huntingdon_railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Cambridge and Huntingdon railway">Cambridge and Huntingdon railway</a> to a new park and ride site south of the town, where it becomes guided. The buses stop at <a href="/wiki/Swavesey" title="Swavesey">Swavesey</a>, Longstanton, <a href="/wiki/Oakington" title="Oakington">Oakington</a> and <a href="/wiki/Histon" class="mw-redirect" title="Histon">Histon</a>, with a request stop for the nature reserve at <a href="/wiki/Fen_Drayton" title="Fen Drayton">Fen Drayton</a>.  Should a proposed <a href="/wiki/New_town" class="mw-redirect" title="New town">new town</a> at Northstowe be built, further stops would be opened, with the Northstowe developers Gallagher Construction being encouraged to build the busway through the development beforehand.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Upon entering Cambridge the route diverges. One route has stops at <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Regional_College" title="Cambridge Regional College">Cambridge Regional College</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Science_Park" title="Cambridge Science Park">Cambridge Science Park</a>, before it rejoins the road network into central Cambridge. The other joins the road network at <a href="/wiki/Orchard_Park,_Cambridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Orchard Park, Cambridge">Orchard Park</a> (formerly Arbury Park), before continuing to the city centre. The two forks converge at Cambridge bus station for the journey to <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_railway_station" title="Cambridge railway station">Cambridge railway station</a>.  Beyond Cambridge railway station the buses are guided along the former <a href="/wiki/Varsity_Line" title="Varsity Line">Cambridge-Oxford railway</a> (The Varsity Line) south to <a href="/wiki/Addenbrooke%27s_Hospital" title="Addenbrooke&#39;s Hospital">Addenbrooke's Hospital</a> and Trumpington Park and Ride. This section last saw a scheduled passenger train in 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-detailed-map_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-detailed-map-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guided-busway.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Guided-busway.svg/220px-Guided-busway.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="275" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Guided-busway.svg/330px-Guided-busway.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Guided-busway.svg/440px-Guided-busway.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="563" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Guided-busway.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wheel-on-kerb method: on the guideway, small wheels touching the kerbs keep the buses in the centre and the bus driver lets go of the steering wheel.</div></div></div>
<p>The busway is designed for buses travelling at 55 miles per hour (89&#160;km/h), slowing to 30 miles per hour (48&#160;km/h) where it crosses public highways.<sup id="cite_ref-soc_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-soc-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Bus drivers are asked to drive as they would do on a normal road.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Guidance is achieved using the guidewheel-on-concrete-kerb method, with the busway constructed from pre-cast concrete sections that are 15 metres (49&#160;ft) long and 2.6 metres (8.5&#160;ft) wide.<sup id="cite_ref-B_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-B-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>  Additionally, the guide wheels will aid close positioning at slightly modified bus stops within the on-street sections.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The busway is 6 metres (20&#160;ft) wide, consisting of two 2.6-metre wide tracks separated by a central reservation of 80 centimetres (31&#160;in). Between Cambridge and St Ives there is also a 4-metre (13&#160;ft) wide (maximum) bridleway/maintenance track to one side and a 70-centimetre (28&#160;in) evacuation strip to the other creating a total width of 10.7 metres (35&#160;ft). Where necessary it is narrower; for example through the Trumpington cutting where there is a single busway with a narrower maintenance-only track giving a total width of approximately 6.3 metres (21&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-soc_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-soc-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> In 2010, proposals were made to reduce the width of the bridleway, narrowing it to 3 metres and increasing the height in order to combat flooding.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>  Elevated sections have two evacuation strips at busway level with the bridleway/maintenance track at the base of the embankment.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>  The bridleway is usable by people on foot, bicycle and horse.
</p><p>The 6-metre (20&#160;ft) width of the busway is narrower than the 9.3-metre (31&#160;ft) width of a single-carriageway rural all-purpose road built to 2009 standards (excluding attendant verges and footpaths/cyclepaths in both cases).<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> A conventional road would have been too wide to fit on top of existing railway embankments and across the under-bridges along parts of the route.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>  The maintenance track is either adjacent to the busway on flat land, or to one side at the foot of the former railway embankments—the combined width of the maintenance track and the busway being considerably wider than that of the railway it had replaced.  To negotiate Trumpington Cutting on the southern section, a narrower maintenance track was required, along with the use of a bi-directional <a href="/wiki/Single_track_(rail)" class="mw-redirect" title="Single track (rail)">single track</a> busway in order to fit within the width of the former double-track railway line.<sup id="cite_ref-transport-assessment_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transport-assessment-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>  The southern section will be restricted to single-decker buses.<sup id="cite_ref-transport-assessment_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transport-assessment-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>   In May 2012 the County Council received a petition calling for better night-time lighting for the bridleway alongside the southern section, and the need for this was subsequently acknowledged by the Council.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Work on lighting was completed in autumn 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Services"><span id="Operators"></span> Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guided_bus_opening_day3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Guided_bus_opening_day3.jpg/220px-Guided_bus_opening_day3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Guided_bus_opening_day3.jpg/330px-Guided_bus_opening_day3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Guided_bus_opening_day3.jpg/440px-Guided_bus_opening_day3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1752" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Guided_bus_opening_day3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Stagecoach Route B bus travelling from Cambridge on the first full day of service on the busway, 7 August 2011.</div></div></div>
<p>Two operators, <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach_in_The_Fens" title="Stagecoach in The Fens">Stagecoach in The Fens</a><sup id="cite_ref-Stagecoach20091029_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stagecoach20091029-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Go_Whippet" title="Go Whippet">Go Whippet</a>, committed to buying new buses and running commercial services on the scheme.
The council had previously held talks with Cavalier (Huntingdon and District) and another operator.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
As with all other UK busway schemes, the Council owns the infrastructure, allowing bus operators to use it on their registered services, subject to quality contracts specifying vehicle and service standards (<a href="/wiki/European_emission_standards#Emission_standards_for_trucks_and_buses" title="European emission standards">Euro IV</a> and <a href="/wiki/Low-floor_bus" title="Low-floor bus">low-floor buses</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-transportxtra-waiting-over_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transportxtra-waiting-over-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> During peak hours of 07:00–19:00 Monday–Saturday operators are charged for using the busway.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc-questions_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-questions-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-transportxtra-waiting-over_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transportxtra-waiting-over-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Originally seven buses per hour ran between St Ives and Cambridge Science Park during the day, reducing to hourly in the evenings and on Sundays. Figures published during 2004 by Cambridgeshire County Council proposed that it would begin operation with six buses per hour and build up to 20 buses per hour into Cambridge during peak periods by 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-ExhibitionPanels_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ExhibitionPanels-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2012, a report to Cambridgeshire County Council suggested opening up the operation of the five Park &amp; Ride sites to companies in addition to just Stagecoach Cambridgeshire in a bid to recover some of the £617,000 annual cost.<sup id="cite_ref-havergal-park-and-ride-competition_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-havergal-park-and-ride-competition-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Routes A and B (Stagecoach)</dt></dl>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cambridgeshire_Guided_Bus_interior.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Cambridgeshire_Guided_Bus_interior.jpg/220px-Cambridgeshire_Guided_Bus_interior.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Cambridgeshire_Guided_Bus_interior.jpg/330px-Cambridgeshire_Guided_Bus_interior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Cambridgeshire_Guided_Bus_interior.jpg/440px-Cambridgeshire_Guided_Bus_interior.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="1024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cambridgeshire_Guided_Bus_interior.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Interior of a single-decker Cambridgeshire Guided Busway route A bus approaching <a href="/wiki/Addenbrooke%27s_Hospital" title="Addenbrooke&#39;s Hospital">Addenbrooke's Hospital</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Stagecoach controls 86% of Cambridgeshire's bus services<sup id="cite_ref-havergal-park-and-ride-competition_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-havergal-park-and-ride-competition-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> and runs Routes A and B between St Ives and Cambridge along the busway, with extensions to Huntingdon railway station.  The journey time from St Ives bus station to the Cambridge Science Park is 23 minutes plus 15 minutes into Cambridge city centre, roughly 38 minutes in total.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>  Stagecoach's previous three-times per hour Service 55 between Cambridge and St Ives had been timetabled at 30–37 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>  The promoters of the scheme predicted that journey times via the busway might be more consistent and reliable, due to buses avoiding the busy A14 road.<sup id="cite_ref-ExhibitionPanels_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ExhibitionPanels-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>To operate their services, Stagecoach ordered ten <a href="/wiki/Wright_Eclipse" title="Wright Eclipse">Eclipse/B7RLE</a> single-decker buses, to be manufactured by Wrightbus and <a href="/wiki/Volvo" title="Volvo">Volvo</a>, and ten <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Dennis_Enviro400" title="Alexander Dennis Enviro400">Alexander Dennis Enviro400</a>/<a href="/wiki/Scania_N230UD" class="mw-redirect" title="Scania N230UD">Scania N230UD</a> double deckers. All the specially-branded vehicles are equipped with leather seats, air chill or <a href="/wiki/Air_conditioning" title="Air conditioning">air conditioning</a>, real time information, and free <a href="/wiki/Wi-Fi" title="Wi-Fi">Wi-Fi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Stagecoach20091029_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stagecoach20091029-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>  The new buses were deployed on Stagecoach's other services prior to the opening of the busway, having cost the operator a total of £3 million<sup id="cite_ref-cn-operators-hit-out_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cn-operators-hit-out-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> plus £1 million in staffing and training costs.<sup id="cite_ref-fewer-services_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fewer-services-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Route A operates regular services from <a href="/wiki/Trumpington,_Cambridgeshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Trumpington, Cambridgeshire">Trumpington</a> Park-and-Ride site in the east, via Cambridge City Centre and <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Science_Park" title="Cambridge Science Park">Cambridge Science Park</a>, to St Ives and <a href="/wiki/RAF_Wyton" title="RAF Wyton">RAF Wyton</a> in the west (and vice versa). The route also serves Addenbrooke's Hospital in both directions. At peak times, some services are extended further west to/from <a href="/wiki/Earith" title="Earith">Earith</a> and <a href="/wiki/Somersham" title="Somersham">Somersham</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-R&amp;T_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-R&amp;T-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AB_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AB-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> On weekdays and Saturdays, services on this route run every 15 minutes between Trumpington and St Ives throughout most of the day, with half-hourly extensions to and from RAF Wyton.<sup id="cite_ref-AB_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AB-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Route A previously didn't operate on Sundays however when <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_North_railway_station" title="Cambridge North railway station">Cambridge North railway station</a> opened (21 May 2017), Route A ran on Sundays between Drummer Street and St Ives Park &amp; Ride via Cambridge North.<sup id="cite_ref-AB_38-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AB-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> In 2018, an hourly service to Royston was added to cover the Route 26 which ceased operation when the Route was transferred from Stagecoach Cambridge to Stagecouch in the Fens.
</p><p>Route B operates services from Cambridge City Centre (usually terminating at Drummer Street) in the east, via <a href="/wiki/Orchard_Park,_Cambridgeshire" title="Orchard Park, Cambridgeshire">Orchard Park</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Huntingdon" title="Huntingdon">Huntingdon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peterborough" title="Peterborough">Peterborough</a> in the west (and vice versa). Some peak-time services are extended beyond Huntingdon to and from <a href="/wiki/Godmanchester" title="Godmanchester">Godmanchester</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-R&amp;T_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-R&amp;T-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AB_38-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AB-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> On weekdays and Saturdays, services on this route run every 15 minutes between Cambridge and Huntingdon bus station; alternate services are extended to and from Hitchingbrooke Hospital, while the remaining services either terminate at <a href="/wiki/Huntingdon_railway_station" title="Huntingdon railway station">Huntingdon railway station</a> (hourly) or run through to Peterborough (hourly). The frequency of these services increases at peak times.<sup id="cite_ref-AB_38-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AB-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> On Sundays, services run every 20 minutes between Cambridge and St Ives, with hourly extensions to and from Huntingdon railway station; there is no service to Hitchingbrooke Hospital or to Peterborough.<sup id="cite_ref-AB_38-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AB-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The two routes combine to give 8 buses per hour (1 bus every 7–8 minutes) through the "core section" between Cambridge and St Ives.
</p>
<dl><dt>Route C (Whippet)</dt></dl>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guided_bus_opening_day2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Guided_bus_opening_day2.jpg/220px-Guided_bus_opening_day2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Guided_bus_opening_day2.jpg/330px-Guided_bus_opening_day2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Guided_bus_opening_day2.jpg/440px-Guided_bus_opening_day2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1336" data-file-height="995" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Guided_bus_opening_day2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <i><a href="/wiki/Go_Whippet" title="Go Whippet">Go Whippet</a></i> Route C bus leaving St Ives on 7 August 2011.</div></div></div>
<p>Whippet Coaches operate Route C from <a href="/wiki/Somersham" title="Somersham">Somersham</a> to Cambridge centre using a mixture of rural roads, Cambridge city centre roads and the northern busway between the St Ives park and ride site and the outskirts of Cambridge. Journey time from Somersham to Cambridge city centre is scheduled at 57 minutes, with no Sunday service.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>  Whippet spent a total of £420,000 on three buses (£140,000 each).<sup id="cite_ref-cn-operators-hit-out_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cn-operators-hit-out-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Less than a month after opening Whippet announced that they would adjust their sporadic Sunday service between Cambridge and Somersham, increasing it to one service per hour.<sup id="cite_ref-havergal-tripled_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-havergal-tripled-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of 2016, services on the route operate every 60 minutes from <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_railway_station" title="Cambridge railway station">Cambridge railway station</a> in the east, via Cambridge Science Park, to <a href="/wiki/St_Ives,_Cambridgeshire" title="St Ives, Cambridgeshire">St Ives</a> in the west (and vice versa). This route runs seven days a week, although it does not run during the evenings. Two buses per day (except Sundays) are extended further west, to and from <a href="/wiki/Somersham" title="Somersham">Somersham</a> (albeit taking a different route than Route A), and later on, it went to Fenstanton.<sup id="cite_ref-R&amp;T_37-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-R&amp;T-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-C_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2018, Go Whippet, shortly after the takeover by Ascendal Group, had ceased operation of the C. No replacement routes were created, but the majority of the route (but not to Fenstanton) is covered by Route A.
</p>
<dl><dt>Routes N and D (Stagecoach)</dt></dl>
<p>Operates on the brand new section of the busway from the <a href="/wiki/A1309_road" title="A1309 road">A1309 road</a> to the new <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_North_railway_station" title="Cambridge North railway station">Cambridge North railway station</a>. This route was short lived, and Stagecoach stopped operating this route. Some Route A journeys go (as Route D) to Cambridge North to cover this.
</p>
<dl><dt>Route R (Stagecoach)</dt></dl>
<p>There is also a fourth route, R, which runs as a shuttle service between Trumpington and <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_railway_station" title="Cambridge railway station">Cambridge railway station</a>, avoiding the Addenbrooke's hospital site. This service runs every 30 minutes each way, on Mondays to Fridays, at peak times only.
</p>
<dl><dt>Routes U and P (Whippet)</dt></dl>
<p>In July 2016 Whippet Coaches launched Route U (for <i>Universal</i>), running on weekdays only from (at first) <a href="/wiki/Madingley_Road" title="Madingley Road">Madingley Road</a> Park-and-Ride and (later) <a href="/wiki/North_West_Cambridge_development#Eddington" title="North West Cambridge development">Eddington</a> to <a href="/wiki/Addenbrooke%27s_Hospital" title="Addenbrooke&#39;s Hospital">Addenbrooke's Hospital</a> and subsidised by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">University of Cambridge</a>. This service runs every 15 minutes on weekdays and was rerouted in December 2016 via the southern section of The Busway between <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_railway_station" title="Cambridge railway station">Cambridge railway station</a> and Addenbrooke's (<a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Biomedical_Campus" title="Cambridge Biomedical Campus">Cambridge Biomedical Campus</a>), via the same loop as Stagecoach route A. For this service Whippet added seven <a href="/wiki/Volvo" title="Volvo">Volvo</a>/<a href="/wiki/Wright_Eclipse" title="Wright Eclipse">Wright Eclipse</a> single-decker buses, with <i>Universal</i> branding in blue colours and fitted for use on The Busway, to the four operating on Route C.
</p><p>In February 2019, in addition to service U, Whippet launched a 4-buses-an-hour service, route P (with <i>Pedigree</i> branding), between Cambridge City Centre (Drummer Street bus station) and Addenbrooke's via the Guided Busway, thus duplicating Stagecoach's A and D services on this section. At rush hours, some journeys run through from or to Swavesey, using the northern part of the Guided Busway.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ticketing">Ticketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Ticketing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On the busway passengers are required to purchase their tickets before boarding<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> from one of seventeen ticket issuing machines compatible with <a href="/wiki/Integrated_Transport_Smartcard_Organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Integrated Transport Smartcard Organisation">ITSO</a> smartcards.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Cambridgeshire County Council stated that multi-operator ticketing would be supported, allowing passengers to board the first bus that arrived, stating that such a ticket would be a first, but would take a while to perfect. Single tickets from one operator will not be valid on another operator's bus, but a multi-operator smartcard can be purchased.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Planning">Planning</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Planning">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2001 the Cambridge-Huntingdon Multi-Modal Study (CHUMMS) recommended widening of the <a href="/wiki/A14_road_(England)" title="A14 road (England)">A14 road</a> and building a guided busway along the old <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_and_Huntingdon_railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Cambridge and Huntingdon railway">Cambridge and Huntingdon railway</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
which had been closed to passengers since 1970 and to all traffic since 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-swavesey_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-swavesey-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Since closure there had been proposals to reinstate the rail service, and for a light railway network, a bus lane, a road with limited access, a bus-way, a cycle path and a nature walk.<sup id="cite_ref-swavesey_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-swavesey-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> A local group, CAST.IRON, was set up in July 2003 after being inspired by the <a href="/wiki/Wensleydale_Railway" title="Wensleydale Railway">Wensleydale Railway</a> to promote and undertake reinstatement of the route for trains and to resist other proposals, referring to the guided bus as the 'misguided bus'.<sup id="cite_ref-libdem_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-libdem-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> A private consortium that had proposed a guided bus scheme, SuperCAM, abandoned their plans in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-rapid-transit-system_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rapid-transit-system-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Arup_Group_Limited" class="mw-redirect" title="Arup Group Limited">Arup</a> prepared the <a href="/wiki/Transport_and_Works_Act_1992" title="Transport and Works Act 1992">Transport and Works Act</a> (TWA) application presented in late 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Public_inquiry" title="Public inquiry">public inquiry</a> was held in September–October 2004. The scheme was supported by five bus and coach operators, and 20 other organisations and individuals.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> A total of 2,735 objections were received:<sup id="cite_ref-soc_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-soc-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> from local councils, public bodies, transport interests, local pressure groups and individuals who criticised the <a href="/wiki/Environmental_Impact_Assessment" class="mw-redirect" title="Environmental Impact Assessment">Environmental Impact Assessment</a>, supported the rail alternative or objected to the scheme in principle.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The scheme was approved by the Government in December 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Construction">Construction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Construction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In March 2007, the then <a href="/wiki/Transport_Secretary" class="mw-redirect" title="Transport Secretary">Transport Secretary</a> <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Alexander" title="Douglas Alexander">Douglas Alexander</a> officially opened a manufacturing plant at Longstanton that would produce the 6,000–7,000 concrete beams for the busway.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-stagg_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stagg-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Each beam was 350 millimetres thick with a further 180-millimetre lip for the glide wheels to press against.<sup id="cite_ref-stagg_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stagg-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> A total of 50,000 tonnes of concrete was cast to a precision of plus or minus one millimetre.<sup id="cite_ref-stagg_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stagg-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Supports below the beams were under-pinned by 2,150 piles along a 2.5 miles (4&#160;km) length of the busway.<sup id="cite_ref-piles_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-piles-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the same year a <a href="/wiki/Viaduct" title="Viaduct">viaduct</a> of maintenance-free <a href="/wiki/Steel" title="Steel">steel</a> was built over the <a href="/wiki/River_Great_Ouse" title="River Great Ouse">River Great Ouse</a> as a replacement for the 200-tonne wrought-iron railway viaduct removed in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> There would later be a dispute between the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative</a>-controlled County Council and opposition <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrat</a> councillors as to whether the structure was structurally sound,<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> with a claim that water draining off the track over the viaduct could lead to crumbling.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway_works.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway_works.JPG/170px-Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway_works.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway_works.JPG/255px-Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway_works.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway_works.JPG/340px-Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway_works.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2112" data-file-height="2816" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway_works.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Construction work under way near Histon, Cambridgeshire in 2008.</div></div></div>
<p>In March 2008 existing guided vehicles were trialled along a section near Oakington.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The vehicles tested included a <a href="/wiki/Wrightbus" title="Wrightbus">Wrightbus</a>-bodied <a href="/wiki/Single-decker_bus" class="mw-redirect" title="Single-decker bus">single decker</a> owned by <a href="/wiki/FirstGroup" title="FirstGroup">FirstGroup</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Plaxton_President" title="Plaxton President">Plaxton President</a>-bodied <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Trident_2" title="Dennis Trident 2">Dennis Trident 2</a> <a href="/wiki/Double-decker_bus" title="Double-decker bus">double decker</a> from <a href="/wiki/Lothian_Buses" title="Lothian Buses">Lothian Buses</a>, and a white <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Dennis_Enviro500" title="Alexander Dennis Enviro500">Alexander Dennis Enviro500</a> <a href="/wiki/Multi-axle_bus" title="Multi-axle bus">triple-axled</a> double decker. The test vehicles were fitted with sensors to assess vibration levels and ride quality.
Hot weather testing of the track took place during May/June 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
In addition to the bus fleet, Cambridgeshire County Council trialled and purchased a specially adapted "guided <a href="/wiki/Gritter" class="mw-redirect" title="Gritter">gritter</a>" lorry for use during periods of cold weather, which will spray salt water rather than <a href="/wiki/Rock_salt" class="mw-redirect" title="Rock salt">rock salt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-havergal-multihog_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-havergal-multihog-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbc-multihog_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-multihog-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>  In November 2011 this was augmented with a customised "Multihog" gritter/snowplough vehicle from Ireland designed for clearing the accompanying maintenance track and cycleway.<sup id="cite_ref-havergal-multihog_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-havergal-multihog-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbc-multihog_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-multihog-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-havergal-multihog-75k_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-havergal-multihog-75k-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The Multihog is powered by 90-horsepower engine allowing it to travel at up to 25&#160;mph (40&#160;km/h) and features a brine tank, rather than solid grit.<sup id="cite_ref-havergal-multihog-75k_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-havergal-multihog-75k-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By August 2008 approximately 6 miles (10&#160;km) of the busway had been constructed, between Longstanton and Milton Road (Science Park).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>  On 30 November 2009, road signs directing traffic from the A14 towards the future busway park and ride sites started to be installed.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>  Other signage related to the busway had required subsequent height adjustments,<sup id="cite_ref-explains-hitches_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-explains-hitches-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> and spelling corrections.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc-spelling_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-spelling-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-telegraph-spelling_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph-spelling-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-camnews-spelling_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-camnews-spelling-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mail-spelling_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mail-spelling-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-upi-spelling_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-upi-spelling-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Trees had also blown over, blocking the busway route near Swavesey.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> The twelve junctions on the route fitted with <a href="/wiki/Bus_priority" title="Bus priority">bus priority</a> traffic signals were tested on 16 December 2010 and worked as expected.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Delays">Delays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Delays">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Waiting_for_the_bus_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2407841.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Waiting_for_the_bus_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2407841.jpg/220px-Waiting_for_the_bus_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2407841.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Waiting_for_the_bus_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2407841.jpg/330px-Waiting_for_the_bus_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2407841.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Waiting_for_the_bus_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2407841.jpg/440px-Waiting_for_the_bus_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2407841.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Waiting_for_the_bus_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2407841.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Concrete beam construction of the main busway route. An estimated 6,000 to 7,000 concrete beams were made for the busway.</div></div></div>
<p>In January 2009 it was announced that the scheduled opening of the scheme had been delayed until late summer 2009 owing to bad weather and flooding in the <a href="/wiki/Fen_Drayton" title="Fen Drayton">Fen Drayton</a> area. As a result of complications with a bridge at <a href="/wiki/Hills_Road" class="mw-redirect" title="Hills Road">Hills Road</a> in Cambridge, traffic restrictions there continued throughout the summer of 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-camnews20090112_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-camnews20090112-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>  Flooding and drainage issues affected the limestone-covered cycleway during late 2009<sup id="cite_ref-camnews20091112_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-camnews20091112-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> and early 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2009 a further delay until late November 2009 was announced for the opening of the northern section, with no date given for the  southern section.<sup id="cite_ref-cracks-not-a-problem_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cracks-not-a-problem-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cow_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cow-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 16 November 2009 the project was delayed for the third time when Cambridgeshire County Council announced that the northern section would not open on the previously advertised date of 29 November 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-CEN20091116_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CEN20091116-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>  An opening date of "the end of the year" 2009 for the northern section was announced later in the same month,<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> followed four days later by "hopefully in the new year [2010]".<sup id="cite_ref-explains-hitches_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-explains-hitches-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>  Initial busway services would only reach <a href="/wiki/Huntingdon_railway_station" title="Huntingdon railway station">Huntingdon railway station</a> and not serve <a href="/wiki/Hinchingbrooke_Hospital" title="Hinchingbrooke Hospital">Hinchingbrooke Hospital</a> as had originally been promoted during the public inquiry;<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> neither would they continue southwards to Cambridge railway station.
</p><p>In January 2010, the contractors and Cambridgeshire County Council were still in discussions about what required finishing.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
During February 2010 the directors of both the signed-up bus operators—Andy Campbell of Stagecoach in Cambridge, and Peter Lee of Whippet coaches—expressed their companies' frustrations at the busway not being usable by the new buses they had bought to run on it.<sup id="cite_ref-cn-operators-hit-out_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cn-operators-hit-out-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>  Shortly afterwards Stagecoach altered the slogan displayed on their fleet of buses for the busway, changing it from reading "I'll be on the busway soon, will you?" to a new slogan of "Will I be on the busway soon?".<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>  In the same month, <a href="/wiki/South_Cambridgeshire" title="South Cambridgeshire">South Cambridgeshire</a> District Council demanded of Cambridgeshire County Council  a comprehensive public statement giving clarity over rising costs.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>  In mid-June 2010, none of the listed outstanding issues had been fixed<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> and a public review was announced.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the start of July 2010, it was reported that neither section would open before 2011;<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> the bus operators reacted to the news angrily, suggesting that they might seek to reduce the minimum level of service that had been previously committed to.<sup id="cite_ref-fewer-services_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fewer-services-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>  At a council meeting on 9 July 2010, a decision was taken to concentrate on completion of the southern section in order to get the whole route opened, rather than aiming for a phased introduction.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
During late September 2010 <a href="/wiki/BAM_Nuttall" title="BAM Nuttall">BAM Nuttall</a> missed deadlines for providing construction certificates needed by the Council, forcing it to begin its own inspections.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trials">Trials</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Trials">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guided_bus_opening_day.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Guided_bus_opening_day.jpg/220px-Guided_bus_opening_day.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Guided_bus_opening_day.jpg/330px-Guided_bus_opening_day.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Guided_bus_opening_day.jpg/440px-Guided_bus_opening_day.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="1720" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Guided_bus_opening_day.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Stagecoach Route B bus prepares to depart from St Ives to Cambridge on the launch day 7 August 2011.</div></div></div>
<p>On 21 April 2011 the busway was officially handed over to Cambridgeshire County Council, triggering a 28-day period for any remedial works be undertaken by BAM Nuttall.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc-handover_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-handover-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> This period expired without BAM Nuttall having completed any of the required work. The County Council contracted Jackson Civil Engineering to finish the busway, at BAM Nuttall's expense, with a view to opening the busway in August 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> The County Council served a legal notice on BAM Nuttall that they were not willing to pay for the budget overrun.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A number of preview trials of the busway were held, during which some problems were encountered, particularly with cyclists using the busway.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> In one incident a cyclist cycling on the guide beams, rather than the cycle path next to the busway, was struck by a bus.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> Trials of recovery procedures should a bus break down were also held, with the test finding that a stranded bus could be connected up and removed within five to ten minutes of a specially-adapted breakdown vehicle reaching the scene.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> During one preview journey held for journalists on 28 July 2011, Hugh Morris of the <i>Cambridge First</i> newspaper staged a race between the guided bus and a car travelling from Cambridge to St Ives to see which was quickest to reach the end of the track. The car beat the bus by ten minutes, although he noted that the trip had not been held during rush hour, during which the A14 road is noted for congestion.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> A journey from St Ives to the Cambridge Science Park was found to take 20 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcopens_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcopens-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Operation">Operation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Operation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Car_traps_on_Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Car_traps_on_Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway.JPG/220px-Car_traps_on_Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Car_traps_on_Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway.JPG/330px-Car_traps_on_Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Car_traps_on_Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway.JPG/440px-Car_traps_on_Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Car_traps_on_Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Car traps</div></div></div>
<p>The busway and cycle track officially opened to the public on 7 August 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcopens_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcopens-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cn-opens_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cn-opens-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> The first guided bus left St Ives at 09:00 after the busway had been opened by <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Lansley" title="Andrew Lansley">Andrew Lansley</a> MP.<sup id="cite_ref-cn-opens_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cn-opens-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> In the first seven days, 55,895 trips were made,<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> leading to the operators providing additional buses on their services.<sup id="cite_ref-hunts-post-demand_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hunts-post-demand-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>  Over the first four weeks the average was 52,227 journeys (224,054 total).<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
Footfall and trade at businesses in the villages increased as a result,<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> with the same increase reported by market traders and shopkeepers in St Ives<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> As a <a href="/wiki/Bridleway" class="mw-redirect" title="Bridleway">bridleway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Horse_rider" class="mw-redirect" title="Horse rider">horse riders</a> can also use the maintenance track adjacent to the northern guided section providing a traffic-free route between the villages.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Work began at the end of July 2011 on improving the park and ride facilities at Longstanton.  Construction work included a £430,000 passenger waiting room and exhibition centre, for the adjacent Northstowe development.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>  The co-building subsequently won an award at the 2012 Green Apple Built Environment and Architectural Heritage Awards.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>  On 12 January 2012, the busway celebrated its one millionth passenger.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The intersections of the busway with the regular roads are equipped with prominently signed "<a href="/wiki/Bus_trap" title="Bus trap">car traps</a>" to prevent motorists driving onto the guide beams and interfering with the bus traffic.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Expansion">Expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>An extension of the busway, to meet the new <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_North_railway_station" title="Cambridge North railway station">Cambridge North railway station</a>, was started in July 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> The authority already had the necessary powers to build the extension.<sup id="cite_ref-transportxtra-waiting-over_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transportxtra-waiting-over-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Originally scheduled to be open in December 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-railwaygazetteJan14_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-railwaygazetteJan14-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> the railway station linked to the busway opened in May 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-cno20160121_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cno20160121-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Construction_costs">Construction costs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Construction costs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cambridge_Guided_Busway_south_rail_bridge_construction.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Cambridge_Guided_Busway_south_rail_bridge_construction.jpg/220px-Cambridge_Guided_Busway_south_rail_bridge_construction.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Cambridge_Guided_Busway_south_rail_bridge_construction.jpg/330px-Cambridge_Guided_Busway_south_rail_bridge_construction.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Cambridge_Guided_Busway_south_rail_bridge_construction.jpg/440px-Cambridge_Guided_Busway_south_rail_bridge_construction.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2176" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cambridge_Guided_Busway_south_rail_bridge_construction.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Construction of the bridge over the railway line near Addenbrooke's Hospital, September 2008.</div></div></div>
<p>The project was budgeted to cost <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">£</a>116.2&#160;million,<sup id="cite_ref-CCC07-03-05_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CCC07-03-05-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> with central government providing £92.5&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>  <a href="/wiki/Cost-benefit_analysis" class="mw-redirect" title="Cost-benefit analysis">Cost-benefit analysis</a> of the scheme had variously assessed the expected ratio as 4.84,<sup id="cite_ref-sand_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sand-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> 2.28 (1998 prices)<sup id="cite_ref-soc_18-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-soc-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> and 1.968,<sup id="cite_ref-sand_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sand-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> (a higher ratio is better), with the cost rising from an initial estimate of £54&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-sand_134-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sand-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> In December 2008, the County Council assessed the financial risks of the project as "high"; None of the £12.7&#160;million funding—out of £23.7&#160;million—due to come from property developers had been received by the promoters.<sup id="cite_ref-camnews-financial_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-camnews-financial-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> In November 2009 the backers of the "cb1" redevelopment scheme around <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_railway_station" title="Cambridge railway station">Cambridge railway station</a> frontage, Ashwell Property Group, had been due to make their £927,000 contribution towards the busway scheme, but were given permission to defer, and entered administration in December 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>  The taxpayer was expected to have to make up any funding shortfall.<sup id="cite_ref-camnews-financial_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-camnews-financial-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>  Cambridgeshire County Council announced it was budgeting £1&#160;million per year to cover potential ongoing costs associated with the busway,<sup id="cite_ref-lgc_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lgc-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-elliott-millions_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elliott-millions-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> through the reorganisation of other transport related budgets.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Repayments for the loans and associated interest would then be recovered from the contractors and future housing developers after the scheme had been completed.<sup id="cite_ref-cn-borrowing_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cn-borrowing-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
Contributions from developers were also used to pay for artworks and <a href="/wiki/Time_capsule" title="Time capsule">time capsules</a> along the route.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph-artwork_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph-artwork-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="BAM_Nuttall_dispute">BAM Nuttall dispute</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: BAM Nuttall dispute">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guided_bus_Oakington_to_Longstanton.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Guided_bus_Oakington_to_Longstanton.jpg/170px-Guided_bus_Oakington_to_Longstanton.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="182" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Guided_bus_Oakington_to_Longstanton.jpg/255px-Guided_bus_Oakington_to_Longstanton.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Guided_bus_Oakington_to_Longstanton.jpg/340px-Guided_bus_Oakington_to_Longstanton.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="2472" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Guided_bus_Oakington_to_Longstanton.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The busway between Oakington and Longstanton. The cycle path is visible on the left of the image.</div></div></div>
<p>In 2008, <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Nuttall" class="mw-redirect" title="Edmund Nuttall">BAM Nuttall</a> claimed that it would cost more than the original budgeted amount to finish the work,<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> perhaps £6&#160;million more.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> Another report<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> suggests that the overrun could be £30&#160;million on a construction cost of £90&#160;million.  Cambridgeshire County Council stated that it had been confident that the scheme would come in on budget because of the terms of its contract with BAM Nuttall.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>  By December 2009, the project had been forecasted to be £1.3&#160;million over budget,<sup id="cite_ref-lgc_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lgc-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-elliott-millions_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elliott-millions-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-telegraph-artwork_141-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph-artwork-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> the Council's extra liabilities being limited to £5&#160;million over the originally agreed price<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>—with the right to impose penalties upon the contractors for late delivery;<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> since February 2009, the contractors had been amassing a fine of £14,000 per day for late delivery,<sup id="cite_ref-cn-operators-hit-out_35-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cn-operators-hit-out-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cn-14k_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cn-14k-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> amounting to £6 million by June 2010<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> and estimated in December 2010 to be £9 million.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> On 29 January 2010, Cambridgeshire County Council's head of audit and risk management stated that uncertainty over the final construction price had been causing <a href="/wiki/Cash_flow" title="Cash flow">cash flow</a> issues for the council.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The County Council's performance bond with BAM Nuttall was limited to £7.5 million, plus a further "unlimited guarantee" from <a href="/wiki/Koninklijke_BAM_Groep" class="mw-redirect" title="Koninklijke BAM Groep">Koninklijke BAM Groep</a>, BAM Nuttall's parent company based in The Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The original price for the engineering works conducted by BAM Nuttall had been £88 million, and estimates in mid-February 2010 projected costs to have increased to £120 to 140 million.<sup id="cite_ref-hunts-stand-off_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hunts-stand-off-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> The main issue was structural repairs necessary to the new Great Ouse Viaduct to prevent water ingress.<sup id="cite_ref-hunts-stand-off_154-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hunts-stand-off-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>  Later that month, Cambridgeshire County Council stated that the council was due to borrow £41 million during 2010 and then £10.2 million the year after, payable to BAM Nuttall in order to complete the project.<sup id="cite_ref-cn-borrowing_140-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cn-borrowing-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cambridgeshire County Council brought in <a href="/wiki/Atkins_(company)" title="Atkins (company)">Atkins</a> as consultants to manage the project.  Following the delivery delays, Atkins' bill increased from an expected £2.9 million to £9.6 million.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-atkins-triples_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atkins-triples-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> The cost of this would be offset by the £10.8-million fine imposed on BAM Nuttall over the same time-period.<sup id="cite_ref-atkins-triples_158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atkins-triples-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A court date of January 2014 was scheduled for proceedings to begin at the <a href="/wiki/Technology_and_Construction_Court" title="Technology and Construction Court">Technology and Construction Court</a> in London. Cambridgeshire County Council stated that it had set aside £6.5&#160;million for legal costs for pursuing the £60&#160;million claim against BAM Nuttall.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>  In May 2012 BAM Nuttall launched a £43-million <a href="/wiki/Counterclaim" title="Counterclaim">counterclaim</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> On 30 August 2013, Cambridgeshire County Council announced that it had reached an <a href="/wiki/Out_of_court_settlement" class="mw-redirect" title="Out of court settlement">out of court settlement</a> with BAM Nuttall.,<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> paying them £84.7 million, up from the £83.9 million original fee. Legal costs and other charges would set the total cost at £152 million,  £26 million of which would have to come from the Council budget.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_proposals">Future proposals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Future proposals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In October 2017 tests began with a ten-seater driverless micro bus running on the grade-separated section from Cambridge railway station to Trumpington Park and Ride.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc-20171016_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-20171016-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
Further expansions to the busway itself have been proposed.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cambourne_and_West_Cambridge">Cambourne and West Cambridge</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Cambourne and West Cambridge">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greater_Cambridge_Partnership&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Greater Cambridge Partnership (page does not exist)">Greater Cambridge Partnership</a> is consulting on a new busway to the west from Grange Rd (March 2019).<sup id="cite_ref-County_Council_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-County_Council-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Southern_extensions">Southern extensions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Southern extensions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cambridgeshire County Council has proposed extending the busway beyond each of the Addenbrooke's Hospital and Trumpington Park and Ride termini.  Funding would be part of the same <a href="/wiki/Transport_Innovation_Fund" title="Transport Innovation Fund">Transport Innovation Fund</a> proposals.<sup id="cite_ref-cambridge-news.co.uk_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cambridge-news.co.uk-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Newmarket_Road">Newmarket Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Newmarket Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During May 2012 proposals were published by the council to provide segregated bus lanes or an extended bus guideway down the central reservation of <a href="/wiki/Newmarket_Road,_Cambridge" title="Newmarket Road, Cambridge">Newmarket Road, Cambridge</a>, between <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_United_F.C." title="Cambridge United F.C.">Cambridge United Football Club's</a> <a href="/wiki/Abbey_Stadium" title="Abbey Stadium">Abbey Stadium</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Road,_Cambridge" title="East Road, Cambridge">East Road, Cambridge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_proposals">Other proposals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Other proposals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In connection with the Chesterton diversion, the CamLink consortium have proposed a busway from the centre of Cambridge, past Cambridge North station to <a href="/wiki/Waterbeach" title="Waterbeach">Waterbeach</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> CamLink is a proposal developed by RLW Estates which is a consortium of The Royal London Group, Turnstone Estates and <a href="/wiki/St_John%27s_College,_Cambridge" title="St John&#39;s College, Cambridge">St John's College</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>CamToo, a transport scheme developed by a separate set of local interest groups,<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> has also offered proposals for further expansion of the guided busway network including:<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Extending the service to operate to Peterborough<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Extension beyond the Milton Road junction, crossing Milton Road to Barnwell Bridge, continuing along the railway alignment already used</li>
<li>New access routes to and from the <a href="/wiki/A14_road_(England)" title="A14 road (England)">A14 road</a> to enable buses from <a href="/wiki/Bar_Hill" title="Bar Hill">Bar Hill</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cambourne" title="Cambourne">Cambourne</a> to access the northern section of the busway and its bridge under the A14 road.</li>
<li>A new bridge under the A14 dual carriageway to enable buses serving Milton, including a new Park and Ride site, to avoid the busy Milton Road / A14 roundabout.</li>
<li>Conversion of bus lanes on Newmarket Road to "tramway" style (bus lanes moved into the centre of the road with right turns across the bus lanes prohibited for normal traffic).</li>
<li>Extension beyond Addenbrooke's Hospital, connecting to the A1303 Babraham Road</li>
<li>Extension beyond Trumpington Park and Ride along the course of the old <a href="/wiki/Varsity_Line" title="Varsity Line">Bedford railway line</a> to the B1046 between <a href="/wiki/Barton,_Cambridgeshire" title="Barton, Cambridgeshire">Barton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Comberton" title="Comberton">Comberton</a>.</li></ul>
<p>In February 2012 a proposal was reported from the Campaign for Better Transport to construct an additional Park &amp; Ride facility at <a href="/wiki/Huntingdon_Racecourse" title="Huntingdon Racecourse">Brampton Racecourse</a> to the north-west of Huntingdon.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Incidents">Incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cambridgeshire_Guided_Busway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the 6 months until January 2013, a total of 20 cars had attempted to drive onto the busway; 18 of these happened at the start of the busway in St Ives at the junction with Harrison Way and the other incidents occurred at various junctions in Cambridge.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> On 5 April 2013, a lorry driver accidentally drove along the busway after following directions given by <a href="/wiki/Satellite_navigation" title="Satellite navigation">satellite navigation</a>. A spokesman for the truck operator concluded that the driver had "relied too heavily on his sat-nav". No damage was caused to the busway and no one was injured. The council warned that the company could be fined if it happened again.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> On 7 February 2019, a lorry became stuck on the busway near <a href="/wiki/Swavesey" title="Swavesey">Swavesey</a> for more than 6 hours after entering at <a href="/wiki/Longstanton" title="Longstanton">Longstanton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A pedestrian was struck and killed as she tried to cross the busway in the dark near to the Fen Drayton Lakes stop on 17 November 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> An inquest into the incident is expected to be held in early 2017.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>. About <span class="frac nowrap"><sup>2</sup>&#8260;<sub>3</sub></span> mile (1&#160;km) south of the Cambridge Railway Station, a tourist was hit by the wing mirror of a passing bus on 11 June 2018 and was taken to hospital with injuries to his leg and shoulders.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> High bus speeds and crowding around the Cambridge Assessment area had been reported, by local councillors, before this incident.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> On 13 September 2018, just a few meters from where the tourist was hit, a cyclist was also struck and killed by a bus on the busway.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Buses on the busway have derailed four times. Two derailments, both in the southern section, were blamed on excessive speed,<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> and the other two, one on the northern and one on the southern section, were blamed by operators on driver error in judging transitions between different parts of the busway.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Other incidents have included one bus crashing into the back of another, following the first braking hard due to horses obstructing the busway,<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> and a collision between a bus and a delivery van at a <a href="/wiki/Level_crossing" title="Level crossing">level crossing</a> at Longstanton.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On the morning of Monday 20th May 2019, a car and a Stagecoach Bus on Route A collided at the intersection near Longstanton. The car burst into flames and the fire spread to the bus, destroying both vehicles. The driver of the bus was injured. The Busway was later reopened at approximately 3.30pm.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
